  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b96eea67-e39e-455c-9f92-030619a6ed9a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText9458272875200889125" style="display:none"><b>HOW FAR WOULD YOU GO? </b><br /><br />All Meg has ever wanted is to get away. Away from high school. Away from her backwater town. Away from her parents who seem determined to keep her imprisoned in their dead-end lives. But one crazy evening involving a dare and forbidden railroad tracks, she goes way too far...and almost doesn't make it back. <br /><br />John made a choice to stay. To enforce the rules. To serve and protect. He has nothing but contempt for what he sees as childish rebellion, and he wants to teach Meg a lesson she won't soon forget. But Meg pushes him to the limit by questioning everything he learned at the police academy. And when he pushes back, demanding to know why she won't be tied down, they will drive each other to the edge -- and over....</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_458162221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458162221" />
    <a title="Nichole * The Book Shredder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5643918-nichole-the-book-shredder"><img alt="Nichole * The Book Shredder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492119065p2/5643918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458162221?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nichole * The Book Shredder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nichole * The Book Shredder" href="/user/show/5643918-nichole-the-book-shredder">Nichole * The Book Shredder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Idiots</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458162221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6680435266428998848">Oh, ho, ho. Brace yourselves, I'm about to write the meanest, most drawn out negative review I've written to date. Be warned though, this review will have cursing. Lots of it, I suspect.<br/><br/>When I read the blurb for <i>Going Too Far</i> I knew I had to read it. Young girl keeps getting in trouble and the cop who's determined to show her the consequences of her actions ends up falling for her? Hell yeah, that sounds hot. And I'm not even the type of person who likes to read books that sound hot. But fuck it</span>
  <span id="freeText6680435266428998848" style="display:none">Oh, ho, ho. Brace yourselves, I'm about to write the meanest, most drawn out negative review I've written to date. Be warned though, this review will have cursing. Lots of it, I suspect.<br /><br />When I read the blurb for <i>Going Too Far</i> I knew I had to read it. Young girl keeps getting in trouble and the cop who's determined to show her the consequences of her actions ends up falling for her? Hell yeah, that sounds hot. And I'm not even the type of person who likes to read books that sound hot. But fuck it because that sounds hot. And I didn't care if their age gap was big enough for statutory rape. (Which it wasn't, <i>lame</i>) <br /><br />I read this book in two very excruciating hours. I skimmed through so much. Oh god, so much skimming. Because the writing is so bad. Not typo ridden bad but written-for-idiots-bad. But if there's one thing that annoyed me to no end in this book, was how many times the author felt the need to tell us that John has dark eyes. Did you guys get that? No? He has dark eyes. In case you didn't get it from the last twenty thousand fucking times she mentioned it. She said it so many times, that I took this e-book and I did a search for the word "dark" and "eyes" to count how many times it happened. I don't care enough to do the math. But the number for dark was 80 the number for eyes was 100. It didn't help that the first time she introduced the fucking eyes she felt the need to describe it as "They were a strangely dark brown in his light face." WHAT THE FUCK IS SO STRANGE ABOUT BROWN EYES IN WHITE PEOPLE? Jesus.<br /><br />Okay so, let's not keep talking about the eyes like Echols did. Because, my god, does she like eyes. Let's talk about the actual story. Let's talk a little about the writing. Let's talk about how my IQ dropped. And about how this book is written for people with an IQ lower than 50, or for kids. And I mean real kids. Not seventeen year olds, but nine year olds who should not be reading about sex. Let's talk about the descriptions. Here's a fantastic one: <br /><br /><i>"The cold March wind kissed my cleavage as he kissed me"</i><br /><br />Isn't that bloody fantastic? The wind kissed her boobs. That's truly amazing. Let's take a look at another one. <br /><br /><i>"I couldn't see him blushing. But I could hear him blushing as his breaths came more quickly"</i><br /><br /> This chick is amazing, really. <br /><br />Let's talk about this chick. Uh, what's her name. Whorelike. The whore. She's a whore. That's what the author chose to do with her. Let's make a whore main character, she said. Yay slut shaming! Because liking sex is bad! YAY! So, this girl likes sex. And she likes smoking pot and sleeping around. And this makes her a slut. Because girls aren't supposed to like sex. Girls are supposed to want relationships. So she's a slut. Oh and she has blue hair. The word blue was mentioned 71 times in this book. Apparently the author thought I would forget that very peculiar trait. <br /><br />Let's talk about the love interest. This guy. He's uh...<br /><br />Let's not talk about him. (And let's not talk about the scene where he tells the main character that smoking pot is way more harmful than cigarettes. Actually lets. "He laughed shortly. “Pot’s a lot more carcinogenic than cigarettes.” HA. Fucktard.) <br /><br />While we're at it, let's talk about how the stupid MC gets angry at him for smoking because she once had cancer, even though it was leukemia (completely unrelated to lung cancer) and she smokes pot, constantly. The fuck, man.<br /><br />This novel has 14,369 ratings and 1,127 reviews and only 1% of them are 1 star reviews and 72% of them are 4-5 star reviews which give this novel an average rating of 4.03 stars. <br /><br /><b> I am convinced this entire world is stupid. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6680435266428998848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer430829209245154736">This was my first time reading Jennifer Echols, I’d seen her book around, but for some reason I never had the initiative to pick on up. Then I saw the cover and synopsis for Going Too Far and I just had to have it. I think originally I’d saw the title as Boy In Blue or something along those lines, but after reading the novel I think that the title, Going Too Far, fits it perfectly.<br/><br/>I was expecting to like this novel, I figured it would be good, what I hadn’t expected was how much I was going to l</span>
  <span id="freeText430829209245154736" style="display:none">This was my first time reading Jennifer Echols, I’d seen her book around, but for some reason I never had the initiative to pick on up. Then I saw the cover and synopsis for Going Too Far and I just had to have it. I think originally I’d saw the title as Boy In Blue or something along those lines, but after reading the novel I think that the title, Going Too Far, fits it perfectly.<br /><br />I was expecting to like this novel, I figured it would be good, what I hadn’t expected was how much I was going to like it! I sat down to read it and I didn’t get up from the couch until I was finished! It was so so... it just sucked me in and would not let go! Meg and John’s relationship was so layered and complex, just wow!<br /><br />I loved Meg’s character, even though she is insane, I got it, I absolutely empathized with her. And John, he may seem one way, but his character is so complex and you don’t really discover that until later in the novel, but I think that is why it works out so well. It’s was addicting. <br /><br />Such a great novel and Echols does a fabulous job in telling it. I’ll definitely be buying a copy to add to my personal library! </span>

<div id="review_34126608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34126608" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1102597-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232412942p2/1102597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34126608?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/1102597-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1102597-ana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34126608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6350485689005154057">This book is clearly a romance. The whole story is about these two different people with their own individual baggage who come together and fall in love. As their relationship develops, you feel like you are on rollercoaster ride -- crazy highs and lows. Their relationship is very charged and, at times, explosive. The sexual tension between them is there from the very beginning and practically on every page there after. These are two people who are very physically attracted to each other but on </span>
  <span id="freeText6350485689005154057" style="display:none">This book is clearly a romance. The whole story is about these two different people with their own individual baggage who come together and fall in love. As their relationship develops, you feel like you are on rollercoaster ride -- crazy highs and lows. Their relationship is very charged and, at times, explosive. The sexual tension between them is there from the very beginning and practically on every page there after. These are two people who are very physically attracted to each other but on such different life trajectories that leaves them both confused about what was happening between them. They were asking of themselves whether it was worth pursuing, did it make it any sense, was there any substance beyond the flirting and attraction, could they let themselves be exposed and vulnerable to the other person...<br /><br />While on the surface they seem to be so different, but as we get to know them, they appear to have a lot in common. For example, they are both very determined, strong, impulsive, defiant, and passionate. I see them in their future relationship as fighting often but having lots of make-up sex. <br /><br />I had different reactions toward finding out the history underling their individual issues. I found Meg's reason for behaving the way she does compelling. She was at a very critical age, developmentally, when faced with her crisis. She had difficulty processing the meaning of it all and her parents weren't all that helpful. I can see why she started having panic attacks and had difficulty coming to terms with what was ahead for her life. I had more difficulty understanding John's backstory. It was harder for me to connect his bridge obsession with the events of 8 years ago when he was so young. It sort of makes sense but I just didn't feel it was enough to justify his current behavior, especially when what he did to Meg when she pushed him to edge...<br /><br />There was no false advertising in the descriptions of this book. They really do push each other to the edge. Amazingly, this is what they each needed in order to move on from the chains of their past. It could have totally backfired but somehow they pulled through and were so much better for it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6350485689005154057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8433623997936197748">This book was HOT! The chemistry and banter between Meg and John (Officer After) could keep me reading for probably a 1,000 pages. It was an absolute pleasure to read I couldn't get enough of it.<br/><br/>Echols writing style is just perfect to me, it's humorous and detailed and random, everything I love. She created a very likable character in Meg, someone who intentionally creates a somewhat shocking appearance (blue hair) and attitude to protect herself but little by little we learn more about Meg and </span>
  <span id="freeText8433623997936197748" style="display:none">This book was HOT! The chemistry and banter between Meg and John (Officer After) could keep me reading for probably a 1,000 pages. It was an absolute pleasure to read I couldn't get enough of it.<br /><br />Echols writing style is just perfect to me, it's humorous and detailed and random, everything I love. She created a very likable character in Meg, someone who intentionally creates a somewhat shocking appearance (blue hair) and attitude to protect herself but little by little we learn more about Meg and the reason she is the way she is and you can't help being on her side and wanting to be her friend. And John, man, I loved reading about this boy. I don't even know what to say.<br /><br />I loved reading about John and Meg on night patrol and watching Meg realize she's falling in love with him. It's pretty cute to see this punk haired bad-a%* girl get kind of self conscious around John. There is a great push and pull between them that keeps you on edge, needing to know where this is going to go.<br /><br />I'm at a loss for words of how to express how much I loved this book! It has so very many things going for it, GREAT characters (main and secondary) a great premise, humor, pain.... just please, do yourself a favor and read this book! I'll definitely be reading the rest of the author's books!<br /><br />And seriously, when can I see the movie version? :P</span>

<div id="review_425517895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425517895" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206058-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481765917p2/5206058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425517895?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/5206058-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206058-kelly?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206058-kelly?shelf=this-is-crap">this-is-crap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425517895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13199898587600958174">Okay so, I've made a vow to myself to write reviews for every book I finish (since making this vow), and the short warning to stay away from this book that served as my review before kept coming back to haunt me, screaming <i>CHEAT!!!</i><br/><br/>I've cooled off since then, so I can probably give a review without dissolving into a puddle of gooey rage and expletives.<br/><br/>First off, let me address the rating; 4.02 average, as of the time I'm writing this review. I'll be honest, it's what reeled me in. And caught me l</span>
  <span id="freeText13199898587600958174" style="display:none">Okay so, I've made a vow to myself to write reviews for every book I finish (since making this vow), and the short warning to stay away from this book that served as my review before kept coming back to haunt me, screaming <i>CHEAT!!!</i><br /><br />I've cooled off since then, so I can probably give a review without dissolving into a puddle of gooey rage and expletives.<br /><br />First off, let me address the rating; 4.02 average, as of the time I'm writing this review. I'll be honest, it's what reeled me in. And caught me like a fish on a hook, in for the same amount of torture. Now I'll admit to being on the outside of a lot of book hype; I was one of the like seven people in the entire world who didn't like <i>Divergent</i>. But I would read a dozen Divergents, two City Of Bones, and top it off with an entire reread of the Twilight saga over subjecting myself to Going Too Far again.<br /><br />Sound harsh? Well, it is. But this is a novel that prompted me to make a whole new shelf to showcase it's absolute crappiness.<br /><br />Now, for the examples; From page one, it becomes evident that the writing is sub-par. Sure, there are a few paragraphs, maybe even an entire page here and there, that don't make your eyes bleed. But for the most part, the writing is overly obvious, the attitudes forced, the descriptions repetitive, and some of them just flat out don't make sense. <i>I couldn't see his face, but I could tell from the way he walked that he was a teenager." "I </i>knew<i> it was too good to be true when it got even better."</i> There is even an instance when Meg can hear John blush. Not hear his blush in his words. <i>Hear John blush.</i> Now I'll forgive a lot, but that is physically impossible.<br /><br />But Meg's sudden bursts of super-human senses weren't even my biggest pet peeves. No, that goes to the most retardedly used, beat-the-reader-over-the-head-with-it metaphor I have ever read.<br /><br />Meg has blue hair. She dyed it awhile ago to stand out or announce her rebelliousness or whatever. And don't worry about forgetting Meg has blue hair or mistaking it for purple or green down the line, because we are <i>reminded</i> of Meg's blue hair. A lot. A whole <i>freaking</i> lot. Even more than we're told about John's dark eyes, we're reminded about Meg's blue hair.<br /><br />And the thing is, she acts like it's a freaking stamp on her forehead proclaiming her a lecher or something. I don't know about you, but I actually think a chick with blue hair is kinda hot. Especially when they're not, you know, thirty. Meg constantly tells herself John can't like her because she has blue hair. When his friends point out the proprietary way he watches her, Meg's internal reaction is this; <i>But my hair is blue!</i><br /><br />Who. The. Eff. Cares?<br /><br />Now, I wouldn't call just why this a metaphor a spoiler, but I'm going to tag it as one anyway just in case. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Meg had a pretty traumatic thing happen in her past. It contributed to her immaturity in some areas, her need to rebel. Her blue hair is supposed to symbolize that immaturity. Hence the metaphor.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Though this one actually is a spoiler, and should only be read if you've already read this book, or are smart enough to heed my warning and don't plan on reading it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Meg dyes it back to her natural brown at the end, her metaphorical growth in maturity, hazzah! Though why she didn't do this in the beginning of the novel when it was clear it was her main cause of self-consciousness is beyond me. Guess that's why there couldn't be a metaphorical tattoo; can't get rid of that with five bucks and a trip to Rite-Aid. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I do not get how this book got so many 4 and 5 star ratings. I really don't. It is one of only two books I've ever rated one star, which should prove that I don't give this rating out lightly.<br /><br />Huh. Looks like I <i>couldn't</i> write this review without dissolving into a puddle of gooey rage. At least I kept the expletives out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13199898587600958174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117588648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117588648" />
    <a title="Greta is Erikasbuddy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3267545-greta-is-erikasbuddy"><img alt="Greta is Erikasbuddy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389224768p2/3267545.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117588648?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greta is Erikasbuddy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greta is Erikasbuddy" href="/user/show/3267545-greta-is-erikasbuddy">Greta is Erikasbuddy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117588648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3904024564267381561">Does anyone remember when my avi looked like this<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695614.jpg' width='240' height='320' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>That is called The Storyteller. It is a fountain that is in the heart of Five Points South in Birmingham. <br/><br/>This story tried to KILL IT!! Ugz!! ok... so, it wasn't the main focus but they talk about the fountain alot at the end of the book and keep referring to it as the DEVIL FOUNTAIN. Dear BOB! I wanted to scream. Only ignorants call it the Devil Fountain. Bahs. It's a statue of a ram man reading stories to his friends of nature. Not reading stor</span>
  <span id="freeText3904024564267381561" style="display:none">Does anyone remember when my avi looked like this<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695614.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>That is called The Storyteller. It is a fountain that is in the heart of Five Points South in Birmingham. <br><br>This story tried to KILL IT!! Ugz!! ok... so, it wasn't the main focus but they talk about the fountain alot at the end of the book and keep referring to it as the DEVIL FOUNTAIN. Dear BOB! I wanted to scream. Only ignorants call it the Devil Fountain. Bahs. It's a statue of a ram man reading stories to his friends of nature. Not reading stories of EVIL. Bahs... and yes yes yes... it does sit in front of a big methodist church but as far as I know... there aren't any protests are anything going on around the statue. No witchcraft either. I just can't stand how this book depicted it like it was a source of evil. <br><br>Ok... rant over. On with my review. (WITH PICTURES!!)<br><br>I had such high hopes for this book. For one it is a MTV book. I've read 2 MTV books: "I wanna be your Joey Ramone" and "Ballads of Suburbia".<br><br>In my opinion they are both better than this book. This book was too fluffy and trying to hard to be bad-ass... and kept upping Birmingham like it was L.A.<br><br>We're not L.A. not even close. <br><br>So, this book is about our BAD-Ass (meg) who gets in trouble and has to run around with a cop her whole spring vacation. 2 of her buds get in trouble too with her but they story doesn't go into great detail about them. The story centers around Meg and her blue hair in a small unnamed town 20 minutes from Birmingham.<br><br>Wait... 20 minutes from Birmingham? Ok... so, I can figure this out right? Well, the story says her and copper (John - who is 19 and a young cop and her woo woo wanna be love interest) have to move cows across the street.<br><br>Cattle? Where on earth can that be? Well, it's in Shelby County.... So, I asked my hubz and we came up with Columbiana.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695615.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><br>I don't know if that's the right town but it's the only place we could think of real close to Birmingham in the right county that might have farm animals.<br><br>The story also talks a heap load about Birmingham Junction. This is the place where all the WRECKS take place. Well, folks... that would be Malfunction Junction... and yup... there are a ton of wrecks there.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695616.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>Apparently the author thinks that everyone high schooler in Jefferson/Shelby Country dream about going to UAB. (University of Alabama Birmingham) Well, we have a ton of those trade school deals and I guess UAB is the closest UNIVERSITY (but we have like 5 Jeff State branches)... but I'm not sure if EVERYBODY wants to go there. It's not THAT snazzy. I guess it's snazzy to ALabama lolz. But it's mainly a medical school (just so ya know -- there's other things but that's why the hospital is named after it)<br><br>UAB campus<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695617.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><br>UAB Hospital<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695618.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><br><br>With all this talk about UAB... the author not once talks about the evil statue the have for the mascot? Yeah.... It's a bit SATANIC!! (muahhahahs!)<br><br>Blaze - mascot for the UAB Blazors (it's a dragon)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695619.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just had the hardest time getting into this book. It was a fun read, I guess but if you know the town the CRYPTIC Code for the sites was nervewracking. OH! And the talk about Condaleza Rice at a college party? Cuz she grew up in Birmingham. My dear pets... this book was published in 2009 during the Obama Administration... not the Bush. Why are we talking about Condy? So, that frustated me. OH! And then she wants to talk about the governor going to prison. While jeesh.... does she not want to talk about the Birmingham Mayor going to prison too? Or what about HealthSouth? Or what about Natalie Holloway? Condey? Uhh.... that's old!! LOLZ... and college students talking about her? Now, that's just not right.<br><br>The whole big SHA-BAM about the book was the magic of Five Points. Five Points is our little artsy district. And by Artsy I mean that's where you get a tattoo at, and Work Play is down there (concerts), and some snazzy restraunts, but it's not LA!! I don't get what this author was trying to tell you guys. So, I shall show you ;)<br><br>Five Points<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695620.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>OH! There was a roadtrip out of Birmingham!! And what landmark did we see? Why the famous Peach Watertower of Clanton..... but they say it looks like a RUMP. Do you see a Rump? (Sings Peaches song by Presidents of the United States)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695621.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A flashback sends us to Dreamland. (hahas! that's funny) Dreamland is a BBQ that was founded in the back woods of Tuscaloosa. This is the one in Birmingham<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695622.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really wanted to really really like this book but the story line was just too floofy for me. I'm proud that it was written by an ALabama Author and was set in (or around) Birmingham. But it still irks me that Jennifer Echols kept referring to the Storyteller Fountain as evil. It's a beautiful piece of art. It bugs me to death that people can't see the magic in it. We are known as the Magic City, afterall. Lighten up and enjoy the mystery!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695623.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338599i/695624.jpg" width="240" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know I would have liked this story better if it was just for that one little thing. <br><br><br><br>For more information about the Storyteller Fountain go here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bhamonline.com/Storyteller/index.shtml">http://www.bhamonline.com/Storyteller...</a><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3904024564267381561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14479110987642963322">Re-read: HOLLY SHIT I LOVED IT JUST AS MUCH IF NOT MORE AS THE FIRST TIME I READ THIS BACK IN 2011 HBJFGKDAFLKSGHJBFLAN<br/><br/>First time reading it: April 29, 2011<br/><br/>I’m going to say a few things before I start my review:<br/><br/>A long while a go I stopped reading. Not completely but, I was reading a book a week instead of a book a day, there were also books that were taking me three weeks to read!. I was blaming it all on school and thought that my blog and club where the ones consuming my time. I just realized </span>
  <span id="freeText14479110987642963322" style="display:none">Re-read: HOLLY SHIT I LOVED IT JUST AS MUCH IF NOT MORE AS THE FIRST TIME I READ THIS BACK IN 2011 HBJFGKDAFLKSGHJBFLAN<br><br>First time reading it: April 29, 2011<br><br>I’m going to say a few things before I start my review:<br><br>A long while a go I stopped reading. Not completely but, I was reading a book a week instead of a book a day, there were also books that were taking me three weeks to read!. I was blaming it all on school and thought that my blog and club where the ones consuming my time. I just realized that I was just missing the right book. I started the firsts chapters of this book and then I went to do other stuff and I simply couldn’t keep my mind off from the story, it was all I could think of; but I really was busy that day so I had to leave it at that. Yesterday I went back to the book and yesterday I finished it. It had been so long since I felt that hunger for a book. So long since I had connected so deeply with a character even though we shared nothing in common ^^. So a Big Thank to everyone who insisted that I needed to read Going Too Far and for marking it as their favorites, If it weren’t for all those high ratings and reviews I would have never discovered Going Too Far, and would have never re-discovered my huge Love for Reading. Thank You :)<br><br>Now I’ll start my review:<br><br><i>Going Too Far</i> is a story that circles around the relationship between Meg and John. John is a cop that follows the law strictly and never goes out of line, he takes care of everything and watched closely a haunted bridge, a bridge that holds all of his inner demons, to a point where he becomes one himself. And Meg, whom is determined to cross all the lines and break every boundary, if only to prove that she’s living and that she has lived; and also someone who runs and runs. She just wants to get away from everything.<br><br>At the beginning of the book Meg breaks some big rules and so Officer John takes control of the situation, punishing Meg by taking away her spring break and forcing her to spend it with him while he’s on duty. Naturally, she hates him. But through the course of her punishment Meg and John start to develop something. Something maybe close to Friendship? Or is it something more…? <br><br>And so with this <i>thing</i> going on, they start to push each other, further, further. John wanting Meg inside the lines and Meg wanting to push John outside them. Who wins…?<br><br><i>Going Too Far</i> is one of the most amazing books I’ve ever read. What I most Love about it is that it’s not just the girl that has issues. That the guys isn’t 100% fine and it’s going to help her with everything. No, they both help each other out and I just think this is a wonderful book and a must read. <br><br>DON’T borrow it! BUY IT! Just BUY IT! I’m already re-reading it :)<br><br><br><br><a href="http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341520i/697629.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer390825455410939952">I tried reading this one last year and couldn't get into it. The heroine was annoying and immature but I'm so glad I tried it again because I loved it.<br/><br/>Yes, it may be slightly cliched and predictable, BUT it was so easy to read and the character growth was written really well, so much so that I ended up loving the heroine. A small part of me does wish that their sex was written into the story, but that's just cause I'm a dirty perv who wants to read about all John's muscles flexing. In reality, I</span>
  <span id="freeText390825455410939952" style="display:none">I tried reading this one last year and couldn't get into it. The heroine was annoying and immature but I'm so glad I tried it again because I loved it.<br /><br />Yes, it may be slightly cliched and predictable, BUT it was so easy to read and the character growth was written really well, so much so that I ended up loving the heroine. A small part of me does wish that their sex was written into the story, but that's just cause I'm a dirty perv who wants to read about all John's muscles flexing. In reality, I think it fit the story as a whole better that it wasn't.</span>

<div id="review_277993207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277993207" />
    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277993207?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=damn-gorgeous-males">damn-gorgeous-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277993207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13099928777126346738"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Would you believe me if I say I'd put off this book for quite a long time because I thought that a cop guy as the hero in a book is not cool? Well, now that I've read it I realized I was Totally. Freaking. Wrong! Because the whole time, I was swooning and crushing and gushing over John After. He absolutely took a place on my top book boyfriends! And yeah, so much for putting this off because, seriously, from all the books I've read of Jennifer Echols this is the one I so enjoyed the mos</span>
  <span id="freeText13099928777126346738" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Would you believe me if I say I'd put off this book for quite a long time because I thought that a cop guy as the hero in a book is not cool? Well, now that I've read it I realized I was Totally. Freaking. Wrong! Because the whole time, I was swooning and crushing and gushing over John After. He absolutely took a place on my top book boyfriends! And yeah, so much for putting this off because, seriously, from all the books I've read of Jennifer Echols this is the one I so enjoyed the most! <br /><br />It was my first time to encounter a really rebellious heroine and at first I didn't think I would be able to love her but again, I was wrong because I really did love Meg! Meg was a funny, smart, and witty character. I loved her sense of humor, her rebelliousness and being dangerous made her more an interesting character. Her story that caused her to have that kind of attitude was very compelling. It was a bit heart wrenching and through that I was able to understand her completely. John After on the other hand was her opposite. He was this one hot cop who was so disciplined and pretty strict in following rules. He had this weird obsession about the 'bridge' and staying in town. Turns out he had a really bad memory about it and thought that by doing what he's doing it will changed what had happened from the past. <br /><br />I enjoyed those dialogue between the two of them which was really funny, cute and steamy! And whenever John blushes at something he said about Meg, awww, it was just like the cutest thing ever! Haha! But what I loved the most was how this two people met and was able to cure and change each other. It was great to see Meg and John growing and learning, caring and loving each other and eventually letting go of their past. The ending was very heart warming. It was touching and emotional and those few words Meg said was just so beautiful. <br /><br />I would definitely recommend this. This is a touching, wonderful and fun read. Not overly emotional but will still tug strings from your heart. A very good realistic read. :))<br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://bookoverdose.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13099928777126346738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_142989539" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142989539" />
    <a title="Cory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3254923-cory"><img alt="Cory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342223197p2/3254923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142989539?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cory" href="/user/show/3254923-cory">Cory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142989539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18294795508271052781">For the record, I lived in Birmingham,Alabama for three years. Therefor, my opinion of this book might be somewhat biased because I am familiar with the area. Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska' title='Looking for Alaska by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Looking for Alaska</a>, Going Too Far takes place in a small town on the outskirts of Birmingham. <br/><br/>However, unlike John Green, Jennifer Echols doesn't succeed in capturing the feel of a small southern town. This problem was also evident in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_' title='Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beautiful Creatures</a>, a slow paced book with an effeminate male narrator. If setting is a large part o</span>
  <span id="freeText18294795508271052781" style="display:none">For the record, I lived in Birmingham,Alabama for three years. Therefor, my opinion of this book might be somewhat biased because I am familiar with the area. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, Going Too Far takes place in a small town on the outskirts of Birmingham. <br /><br />However, unlike John Green, Jennifer Echols doesn't succeed in capturing the feel of a small southern town. This problem was also evident in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_" title="Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Creatures</a>, a slow paced book with an effeminate male narrator. If setting is a large part of your story, as it is here, I think it would be best to make the story feel true to its setting.<br /><br />That being said, this is a MTV book. Having previewed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2207115.I_Wanna_Be_Your_Joey_Ramone" title="I Wanna Be Your Joey Ramone by Stephanie Kuehnert" rel="nofollow noopener">I Wanna Be Your Joey Ramone</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5930447.Ballads_of_Suburbia" title="Ballads of Suburbia by Stephanie Kuehnert" rel="nofollow noopener">Ballads of Suburbia</a>, I've realized that MTV doesn't publish quality books. But I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22628.The_Perks_of_Being_a_Wallflower" title="The Perks of Being a Wallflower by Stephen Chbosky" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perks of Being a Wallflower</a>, so I was willing to set aside my predetermined notions about MTV books in general. <br /><br />I'm somewhat familiar with Jennifer Echol's books, having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7129588.Forget_You" title="Forget You by Jennifer Echols" rel="nofollow noopener">Forget You</a>. I wasn't too impressed, but I was willing to give Echols another try. I probably won't be reading another one of her books anytime in the future. <br /><br />Echols relies two annoying tropes. The first is the tragic past. Authors give characters tragic pasts in order to excuse them from their flaws. I once fell prey to this trap, not realizing that a character can be complex without having to loose a sibling/parent, having survived cancer, having lived in poverty, or having attempted suicide. <br /><br />This trope irritates me to no end because it's like the author tries to makes you feel bad for not sympathizing with his or her characters. I often felt this way when I was reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439288.Speak" title="Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Speak</a>. Just because I don't feel any sympathy for your character doesn't mean that I advocate rape, murder, or suicide. Quite the contrary. It means that I wish you hadn't used these as cheap plot devices to develop your characters. <br /><br />Or, as is the case in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71332.Push" title="Push by Sapphire" rel="nofollow noopener">Push</a>, if you think the book is bad, you're insensitive to rape victims. Or, because you haven't been raped, you wouldn't understand, making your opinion irrelevant even if the book is bad. <br /><br />If you're familiar with Contemporary YA, then you know of John Green, Sarah Dessen, Elizabeth Scott, and Barry Lyga. The exceptions being, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines" title="An Abundance of Katherines by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">An Abundance of Katherines</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/678891.Bloom" title="Bloom by Elizabeth Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloom</a>, these authors manage to write realistic teens without using too many pop-culture references, dropping the f-bomb on every other page, or making use gratuitous sex scenes. Well, in the case of John Green, your mileage may vary. <br /><br />Around 4/5ths of this novel, I was waiting for it to end. There was nothing that made me want to finish. After the secret was revealed, there was nothing to keep reading for. That's often the problem with having your plot hinge on cheap tropes and devices. Often after the will they, won't they drama dies down and your book jumps the shark, what's left? <br /><br />Like Sarah Dessen, I don't think Jennifer Echols knows much about drugs. I find it somewhat funny, anytime an author has their characters smoke pot to prove that they're hardcore. While actions speak louder than words, in literature this isn't the case. Instead of coming off as badass, Meg comes off as kind of stupid. And once again we are told that characters are intelligent, rather than being shown. Meg and John are supposed to be somewhat intelligent, yet their big aspiration is to go to UAB. My dad graduated from UAB. From what he's told me, there aren't that many spectacularly intelligent people graduating from there. How hard is to remember, <b>show don't tell.</b><br /><br />Romance plays a big part in this book. However, by the time Meg and John acted on whatever meager chemistry they had, I wasn't interested. I didn't have a problem with Meg. Sure, she was annoying at times, and her past was contrived as a means to excusing her from her flaws, but she was funny. I actually found her amusing. John, on the other hand, was kind of possessive and overbearing at times. He wasn't very amusing, and for the first fifty pages I didn't like him very much. Authors these days don't seem to understand what it takes to make a character likable. Rather than reveal why John acts the way he does during the first few pages, Echols waits to reveal the information. By this time, I don't care. This isn't suspenseful, it's annoying. <br /><br />I was also troubled by a few major logic fails. Can John really be an patrol officer that carries a loaded gun at such a young age? I don't think so. He might look forty, but he's still nineteen. Can the town pot head really get away with so much? Can minors be arrested so easily without being read their right?<br /><br />Are all southerners backwards, illiterate, trailer trash morons? No. I have a few relatives that live in Edgewater, Alabma. I can tell you that southerners aren't that dumb. Meg and John aren't the only intelligent people that have graced the southern states. <br /><br />Another issue that I have with all modern YA books set in the south. Alabama is 26.3% black. 12.9% of all black people in the USA live in Alabama. Yet in every single one of these books, there are no black characters. I might believe that this is possible in Connecticut or Delaware, but not in the south. Occasionally, we might give an Asian or two, but this is just ridiculous. <br /><br />Also, the character development in this book is somewhat unbelievable. John and Meg completely transform in twenty pages. Apparently all Meg needs is a strong man in her life to completely change her ways. I don't even know why John liked Meg, outside of her sex appeal. <br /><br />My last complaints are as follows. Apparently Meg sleeps around with the local pot head and John won't sleep with her unless she's completely naked -- he says this is because he wants her trust. Yeah right. And Meg is claustrophobic so this somehow equates with her not wanting to be seen naked, but she'll sleep with anything male that moves. Because this is Echols, I'd say the content in this book is 14+. However, this isn't as graphic as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7129588.Forget_You" title="Forget You by Jennifer Echols" rel="nofollow noopener">Forget You</a>.<br /><br />I wouldn't recommend this book, but I wouldn't say that you shouldn't read it. Just don't read it passively. Be aware of what you're reading and don't accept it as good literature. Fans of Contemporary YA deserve better.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18294795508271052781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_247386270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247386270" />
    <a title="Lissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973484-lissa"><img alt="Lissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442600840p2/4973484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247386270?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lissa" href="/user/show/4973484-lissa">Lissa</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973484-lissa?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973484-lissa?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973484-lissa?shelf=love-this-boy">love-this-boy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247386270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13053494062742214670"><b>Also appears on <a href='http://lissawrites.wordpress.com/2012/05/18/review-going-too-far-by-jennifer-echols/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lissa Writes</a></b><br/><br/><br/>I can't for the life of me come up with any good reason for why this book is 4 stars and not 5 stars. Normally five stars for me are rated for books that have a huge emotional impact or connection, or challenge me (or are just plain and simply awesome, or I read in my childhood and I'm totally nostalgic for). I didn't really have an emotional connection but this book did have an emotional impact on me, because I cried in one particular part near the climax. Still, if </span>
  <span id="freeText13053494062742214670" style="display:none"><b>Also appears on <a href="http://lissawrites.wordpress.com/2012/05/18/review-going-too-far-by-jennifer-echols/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lissa Writes</a></b><br /><br /><br />I can't for the life of me come up with any good reason for why this book is 4 stars and not 5 stars. Normally five stars for me are rated for books that have a huge emotional impact or connection, or challenge me (or are just plain and simply awesome, or I read in my childhood and I'm totally nostalgic for). I didn't really have an emotional connection but this book did have an emotional impact on me, because I cried in one particular part near the climax. Still, if you ask me what you could change about this book to make it 5 stars, I wouldn't be able to tell you. I really liked it, to me it just wasn't amazing. However, I would recommend it to romance readers and people who love contemporary YA.<br /><br />And I think it's a really beautiful novel about two damaged people learning to love and overcome their fears. The romance developed nicely and despite Meg's age (17) it was totally believable.<br /><br />And I totally love Meg's attitude. She's not a bitch, just a rebel with no cause and no fear. John was a giant sweetheart and a total hottie (I don't often find literary characters hot but Echols' descriptions were really great, and I got sucked in to Meg's head to see the attraction) but there was something about him that made me feel that he was a tiny bit manipulative. Maybe it was his protectiveness and his need to CONTROL ALL THE SITUATIONS but he seemed to manipulate Meg a bit, especially physically which is so NOT okay especially as he's this huge cop and she's this tiny teenager.<br /><br />Well sure, the entire plot revolves around John's decision to make Meg ride along with him. And I secretly have a thing for Gothic novels, which abhors the feminist side of me, because the I'd hate to be in the same position myself but there's a reason Belle from Beauty and the Beast was my favourite Disney princess for many years. I like reading about strong girls trapped in an environment with an older dude who has a position of power over her. Don't do that to me in real life, but I kind of like it in my entertainment. It's my guilty pleasure. That's why I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12923.The_Castle_of_Otranto" title="The Castle of Otranto by Horace Walpole" rel="nofollow noopener">The Castle of Otranto</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50398.Northanger_Abbey" title="Northanger Abbey by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Northanger Abbey</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre" title="Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Jane Eyre</a>.<br /><br />Going Too Far isn't a Gothic novel, but it does have the basics of one. Meg often wonders if she's suffering from Stockholm Syndrome because she's being forced to spend time with Officer Hottie.<br /><br />The novel was written okay. I had some issues with the text, mostly because I think they might have been speaking in slang sometimes and I'm not from America, and sometimes the dialogue was ambiguous and vague so it took me a few pages to realise what they were talking about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially when Meg and John made a date to have sex and kept referring to it as 6:01AM Thursday, which was the time Meg's ride along would be over <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But I'm clever enough to work it out in the end, and maybe that's what matters.<br /><br />Pretty much the only problem I had with the book was at the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Meg decided to dye her blue hair back to brunette. I understand why she did it - because the blue dye represented her fight with cancer, and accepting that it was over meant going back to a normal colour. But to me it looks like the shrew has been tamed - that the wild child has settled down. I know characters have to change over the course of novels but I would have liked it if she dyed it a colour that wasn't her natural colour: blonde, or auburn, or even green. The dye represents a change in her attitude but the colour delivers the message to the reader. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If you like contemporary YA romances you'll probably love this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13053494062742214670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_49778197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49778197" />
    <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days"><img alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49778197?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49778197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13950057230842720179">Meg's a wild, rebellious girl who has panic attacks at being confined by as much as a seat belt. Her mother still cries over her and her father has washed his hands of her and her (currently) blue hair. She has just a few months left of high school to go and then she can escape the small town and move to the city to go to uni. And the one thing she's looking forward to before that can happen is the March Break trip to Mexico.<br/><br/>Which is ruined by one night's stupid decision. Along with her pot-addl</span>
  <span id="freeText13950057230842720179" style="display:none">Meg's a wild, rebellious girl who has panic attacks at being confined by as much as a seat belt. Her mother still cries over her and her father has washed his hands of her and her (currently) blue hair. She has just a few months left of high school to go and then she can escape the small town and move to the city to go to uni. And the one thing she's looking forward to before that can happen is the March Break trip to Mexico.<br /><br />Which is ruined by one night's stupid decision. Along with her pot-addled "boyfriend" Eric and two friends from school, Tiffany and Brian, Meg is arrested for trespassing on a train bridge - which killed two kids several years ago. While Eric's hot-shot lawyer father gets him off, the other three are made to spend the March Break week with the ambulance, fire brigade and police - and guess which one Meg gets.<br /><br />Not only does she have to spend five nights on the graveyard shift riding around in a cop car, but she has to spend them with the very same cop who arrested them: John After. John with the "Matt Damon" body, who turns out to be nowhere near as old as Meg had assumed. He chose to stay in the town, to serve and protect and save teenagers from stupid choices, but Meg pushes him to question the things he abides by - and he pushes back. As they both confront each other the chemistry coalesces and thickens, and something new is forged.<br /><br />"Chemistry" is the Big Word for this novel. It has shovel-fuls of it. Meg is a spunky, smart, inherently vulnerable girl with a sharp, hard exterior. John is more complicated than he seems, and the character development is beautifully explored as layers are revealed and they both become very real in your mind.<br /><br />The plot is a simple premise to get these two together, and it has that small-town ring of truth to it; it's the people who are complicated. Narrated by Meg, her voice has that same hard, spiky exterior behind which she hides her compassion and interest in others - you get to know her and yet she keeps you at a distance at the same time. It's John who breaks through that exterior, and him we follow as Meg learns to accept herself. Nothing's easy, of course, and the revelation (one of two; the last one) at the end - while hinted at, or something you could guess - had a similar impact on me as it did on Meg.<br /><br />I have to draw your attention back to the romance and chemistry again. If you, like me, loved <i>Twilight</i> and similar books for the chemistry between the two main characters, and you'd like more of that intense thrill, then you absolutely have to read this. It's not the same, but it has that same quality that breathes off the page. Somewhere out there, John and Meg are living their lives. Sweet and charming, heart-warming and sexy, <i>Going Too Far</i> is a book to read in one sitting: not just because it's a fast read, but because you won't want to put it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13950057230842720179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer18180180963638120097">I intended to just get started on Going too Far and enjoy the book during the weekend. Plans changed... I couldn’t put it down and I finished it in one sitting. What a great book! It’s earned the coveted spot on my bookshelf reserved for re-reads.<br/><br/>I loved the point of view of the book, which was from Meg’s perspective. She’s snarky, dangerous, smart, and endearingly flawed. Her mental dialog is witty and kept me engaged throughout the entire book. In addition, the dialog between Meg and John (Off</span>
  <span id="freeText18180180963638120097" style="display:none">I intended to just get started on Going too Far and enjoy the book during the weekend. Plans changed... I couldn’t put it down and I finished it in one sitting. What a great book! It’s earned the coveted spot on my bookshelf reserved for re-reads.<br /><br />I loved the point of view of the book, which was from Meg’s perspective. She’s snarky, dangerous, smart, and endearingly flawed. Her mental dialog is witty and kept me engaged throughout the entire book. In addition, the dialog between Meg and John (Officer After) was actually pretty steamy at times and fun to read throughout.<br /><br />About the story... Meg and three of her friends get caught one night breaking the law right before spring break. Arrested for public intoxication and trespassing in a restricted zone (a situation that could have resulted in their certain death) all but one of them are put on probation and each are required to ride the night shift for one week with a patrol officer, emergency medical technician and fire fighters to witness firsthand the dangers of poor and/or dangerous situations. <br /><br />When Meg is assigned to Office After, the policeman that arrested them, she’s determined to unnerve him and make him pay for ruining her senior spring break plans. As the week progresses, she learns he’s not that much older than her and they both begin to develop an attraction. She finds herself worrying about him as he faces dangerous situations during his shift. Soon enough, events of their past reveal themselves and they both find each other in a situation they didn’t anticipate.<br /><br />Great book, that’s edgy, fun, steamy and emotional!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18180180963638120097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73390516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73390516" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73390516?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-electronic">own-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73390516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13590354819113740289"><i>Going Too Far</i> delineates the story of Meg and Officer John After. Meg, a high school senior, cannot wait to go to college and escape her backwater town as well as her domineering parents. John decided to stay in the city and fight crime - so when he catches Meg on a dangerous bridge drinking alcohol and doing drugs, the two collide in a way that creates romantic chemistry and sexual tension.<br/><br/><i>Going Too Far</i> was my first MTV book, so I wasn't sure what to expect besides some scandalous stuff going o</span>
  <span id="freeText13590354819113740289" style="display:none"><i>Going Too Far</i> delineates the story of Meg and Officer John After. Meg, a high school senior, cannot wait to go to college and escape her backwater town as well as her domineering parents. John decided to stay in the city and fight crime - so when he catches Meg on a dangerous bridge drinking alcohol and doing drugs, the two collide in a way that creates romantic chemistry and sexual tension.<br /><br /><i>Going Too Far</i> was my first MTV book, so I wasn't sure what to expect besides some scandalous stuff going on. And I hit the nail on the head with that hypothesis - this book is one huge bad girl vs. sexy cop romance story. There was an inundation of descriptions such as "I saw him staring at my chest" or "his huge, sexy muscles". While physical characterization is okay, I would have preferred something deeper than just how attractive the two protagonists were to each other.<br /><br />The rest of the book was lukewarm for me. The writing was average, the characters were average, and there wasn't anything necessarily bad about the book but nothing that made me love it either. It felt like a typical romance novel with a couple of interesting plot twists thrown in.<br /><br />If you're looking for a young-adult love story that doesn't require much thought, <i>Going Too Far</i> may be the book for you. If you're searching for a more in-depth romance novel, I recommend <i>Gone With the Wind</i>, <i>Forbidden</i>, or <i>Shiver</i>.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13590354819113740289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_205393708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205393708" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205393708?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8174563-going-too-far">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205393708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6655715001168686682"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/> <br/><blockquote>
  <i>I wondered what it would be like to see the dark blue sky above us not as heavy drapes of cloth, the top of a circus tent, but as an infinite expanse. As everybody else saw it.</i>
</blockquote> In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4570679.Going_Too_Far' title='Going Too Far by Jennifer Echols' rel='nofollow noopener'>Going Too Far</a>, Jennifer Echols has crafted a compelling story about the connection between two characters who are, in some ways, the very antithesis of each other. <br/><br/>Meg won’t be tied down, literally. Resistant to plans, authority, confined spaces – she combats restrictions and small-town claustrophobia wit</span>
  <span id="freeText6655715001168686682" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /> <br /><blockquote>
  <i>I wondered what it would be like to see the dark blue sky above us not as heavy drapes of cloth, the top of a circus tent, but as an infinite expanse. As everybody else saw it.</i>
</blockquote> In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4570679.Going_Too_Far" title="Going Too Far by Jennifer Echols" rel="nofollow noopener">Going Too Far</a>, Jennifer Echols has crafted a compelling story about the connection between two characters who are, in some ways, the very antithesis of each other. <br /><br />Meg won’t be tied down, literally. Resistant to plans, authority, confined spaces – she combats restrictions and small-town claustrophobia with plans to go away to college and avoidance of emotional entanglements. <br /><br />John After lives within his carefully constructed defences, refusing to be left exposed and vulnerable. A law-enforcer, a rule-abider, Officer After is guarded and cautious. He is the practiced restraint to Meg’s reckless abandon. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4570679.Going_Too_Far" title="Going Too Far by Jennifer Echols" rel="nofollow noopener">Going Too Far</a> is an incredibly engaging read. The chemistry between Meg and John is intense and volatile, the story becoming increasingly charged with each page. The interactions between the characters spark with the friction of conflict and attraction. Add to this the enforced distance of the situation that throws them together, and the plot is heavy with anticipation. <br /><br />Sexual tension aside, it is also an honestly expressed portrayal of what it is to let go, to trust, to be hurt and to hurt someone else. In this respect, Echols has created realistic characters, with flaws and strengths, each contending with their own internal issues. Importantly, whether their actions are sympathetic or not, they act like teenagers: perhaps not always defensible, but mostly understandable. <br /><br />This was my first Echols novel, and I was impressed with the fluid writing and her deft hand with dialogue, particularly with Meg’s snarky, self-deprecating humour. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What’s <i>unimpressive</i> about this book is the distinctly horrid cover. Please don’t let that fool you about what’s inside. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> While a major selling point is clearly the romance aspect, there was also greater substance here than I was expecting, in the exploration of Meg and John as nuanced individuals.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4570679.Going_Too_Far" title="Going Too Far by Jennifer Echols" rel="nofollow noopener">Going Too Far</a> ended up being not quite what I had expected, in a good way. <br /><br />Somewhat surprising, definitely engaging, and highly enjoyed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6655715001168686682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106104295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106104295" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106104295?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
